<span id="freeTextContainer8595294011047704595"><strong>Baby or Bust!<br /><br /></strong>When last seen, Amy Thomas, the mad bride-to-be, was working her way through her 70-item to-do list, trying to keep chicken off the reception menu, and vowing never to change her name. Now Amy Thomas Stewart is a newlywed and a career woman, and becoming a mom is the last thing on her to-do list. So why is Amy obsessing about baby clothes and ogling pregnant w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8595294011047704595"><strong>Baby or Bust!<br /><br /></strong>When last seen, Amy Thomas, the mad bride-to-be, was working her way through her 70-item to-do list, trying to keep chicken off the reception menu, and vowing never to change her name. Now Amy Thomas Stewart is a newlywed and a career woman, and becoming a mom is the last thing on her to-do list. So why is Amy obsessing about baby clothes and ogling pregnant women on the street? <br /><br />Suddenly Amy realizes the inconceivable: She wants a baby—even though she’s just lost her job, their apartment’s way too small, and she doesn’t have a clue as to her ovulation cycle. Caught up in a passion to procreate, Amy knows she has to strike while the iron is hot. And if getting pregnant is making Amy this crazy, just think what will happen when the stick turns blue…</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/13035968" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/808585-kelli" class="left imgcol" title="Kelli"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1323759631p2/808585.jpg" alt="Kelli" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/13035968?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 21, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/808585-kelli" class="user" title="Kelli">Kelli</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer13035968">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6881638982460276646">I didn't think that I could laugh more than I did with "Mad Bride", but this book surpassed it for me. I just could not stop laughing and I had to stop reading in so many various areas in the book to wipe my eyes and catch my breath. It was a great, light, funny read and I read it in one day. I could not put this down.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer59930755">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer940200911656701864">Terrific book for the genre! It wasn't all about "being pregnant" and wasn't all of the shiny happy preggo moments most people deal with. it was the truth! And I repect her for telling it! Its a decent book for a father to be to read to catch a glimpse into the mind of his pregnant wife. I will never get to experience that, but at least I know a little of a few different people's perspectives.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1444266523?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 16, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3506359-brenda" class="user" title="Brenda">Brenda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3506359-brenda?shelf=laugh-out-loud" class="actionLinkLite">laugh-out-loud</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1444266523">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5266009777903145865">“Diary of a Mad Mom-to-Be” by Laura Wolf follows Amy after her wedding in “Diary of a Mad Bride”. Amy is still as hilarious as ever now that she’s expecting a baby. I found “expecting” Amy to be much more enjoyable than “bride” Amy and found myself laughing out loud throughout the book. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/1333177-ciara" class="user" title="Ciara">Ciara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who find a copy laying at a bus stop</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1333177-ciara?shelf=crummy-chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">crummy-chick-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1333177-ciara?shelf=read-in-2006" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2006</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer34978082">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13710424219106647506">all i remember about this book is that the protaganist is preggers. as with the overwhelming majority of chick lit that features a pregnant main character, i often wanted to rip my hair out &amp; claw at my eyes as she inevitably frets over the pregnancy making her too "fat" to wear designer clothes, &amp; yet she totters around on stilettos anyway until the day her water breaks, &amp; she demands lots of pain medication &amp; generally gets really psyched about shopping for baby stuff more than</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13710424219106647506">all i remember about this book is that the protaganist is preggers. as with the overwhelming majority of chick lit that features a pregnant main character, i often wanted to rip my hair out &amp; claw at my eyes as she inevitably frets over the pregnancy making her too "fat" to wear designer clothes, &amp; yet she totters around on stilettos anyway until the day her water breaks, &amp; she demands lots of pain medication &amp; generally gets really psyched about shopping for baby stuff more than she gets psyched about actually having a child. there was probably factually questionable stuff in here, which i still retain from my quick spin through midwifery school several years ago. this was the sequel, i believe, to the book in which the main character gets married, &amp; is a total bridezilla. some people call this kind of book "mommy lit". it's all pretty insufferable, but it's a quick read &amp; it's right up my alley when i have a headache or the weather is awful or i just want to get sucked into someone else's inconsequential problems for a few hours instead of worrying about my own. also, i found it at a bus stop, so it's not like i paid money for it.</span>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_147666078">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147666078" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4368718-melissa" class="left imgcol" title="Melissa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1362753282p2/4368718.jpg" alt="Melissa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/147666078?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 24, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4368718-melissa" class="user" title="Melissa">Melissa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/376605.Diary_Of_A_Mad_Mother_To_Be" title="Paperback 9780752858975" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4368718-melissa?shelf=books-i-adored" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-adored</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368718-melissa?shelf=books-from-library" class="actionLinkLite">books-from-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer147666078">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16889004358248090473"><em>When last seen, Amy Thomas, the mad bride-to-be, was working her way through her 70-item to-do list, trying to keep chicken off the reception menu, and vowing never to change her name. Now Amy Thomas Stewart is a newlywed and a career woman, and becoming a mom is the last thing on her to-do list. So why is Amy obsessing about baby clothes and ogling pregnant women on the street? </em><br /><br />Laura Wolf is amazing; she truly is. Every time I read either <em>Diary of a Mad Bride-to-be</em> or <em>Diary of a Mad Mother-to-b</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16889004358248090473"><em>When last seen, Amy Thomas, the mad bride-to-be, was working her way through her 70-item to-do list, trying to keep chicken off the reception menu, and vowing never to change her name. Now Amy Thomas Stewart is a newlywed and a career woman, and becoming a mom is the last thing on her to-do list. So why is Amy obsessing about baby clothes and ogling pregnant women on the street? </em><br /><br />Laura Wolf is amazing; she truly is. Every time I read either <em>Diary of a Mad Bride-to-be</em> or <em>Diary of a Mad Mother-to-be</em>, I always feel a weight off my shoulders. Her writing is hilarious; her characters likeable. It’s like <em>The Princess Diairies</em> but for mature audiences, and with a less whiny protagonist. <br /><br />This time around, Amy Thomas Stewart decides she wants to have a baby and with her copy of <em>Baby How, Baby Now</em>, she gets ready to tackle that brave new world. Only, Amy is still Amy and <em>Baby How, Baby Now</em> is just this new installment’s version of <em>Beautiful Bride</em>. Will she ever make it out sane?<br /><br />I love Amy. She’s funny, witty, and very relatable. I couldn’t help but find myself giggling as I read about her adventures towards motherhood. The best thing is that in this sequel, Amy is now in the PR business and it’s an industry I myself working in the future. It was amusing to read her experiences and the things she has to deal with on that note as well. <br /><br />Another great thing about <em>Diary of a Mad Mother-to-be</em> is that it also continues the story of the secondary characters. Sure, it isn’t in detail, but it’s nice to know how Mandy, Anita, Misty, Gram and company are all doing. New characters are also introduced and they were a real hoot to the story.<br /><br />I really can’t sing enough praises for <em>Diary of a Mad Bride-to-be</em> and <em>Diary of a Mad Mother-to-be</em>, so if you’re looking for an easy, relaxing, hilarious read, be sure to try these two. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16889004358248090473">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/177861960?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 18, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5550243-rebecca" class="user" title="Rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5550243-rebecca?shelf=chicklit" class="actionLinkLite">chicklit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer177861960">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1697491061726130855">I enjoyed the previous book by this author and this was a follow up, which I didn’t know existed, so when I saw it, I immediately picked it up. As usual, I like the first one better, but this one was okay too. Half the book was taken up with pointless lists that just repeated them selves, with more stuff just crossed out and it was written in diary format, so it was super easy to breeze through and also read during commercials on TV, which is always a plus for me. Gee, I wonder what this book is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1697491061726130855">I enjoyed the previous book by this author and this was a follow up, which I didn’t know existed, so when I saw it, I immediately picked it up. As usual, I like the first one better, but this one was okay too. Half the book was taken up with pointless lists that just repeated them selves, with more stuff just crossed out and it was written in diary format, so it was super easy to breeze through and also read during commercials on TV, which is always a plus for me. Gee, I wonder what this book is about! I didn’t like where this book started, how the girl and dude, didn’t really care about kids and weren’t in a rush to have them and then like all of a sudden, the girl is like, I must have kids NOW. Seriously, that came out of nowhere! And the parents and grandmother! So annoying, it’s like, ohmigod, just cut those people out of your life! It will be so much better otherwise! But I like that the guy is kind of in the background and doesn’t have much personality, which is usually kind of annoying, but in this format and these books, it works. You don’t really care. End note: lame, but entertaining.<br /><br />Grade: C</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1697491061726130855">...more</a>

          </span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1498680.Diary_of_A_Mad_Mom_To_Be" title="Paperback 9792220011" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

              <a href="/review/list/114114-ferina?shelf=chicklit" class="actionLinkLite">chicklit</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer3014730">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4930606708071853208">Di awal-awal pernikahannya, pasangan Amy dan Stephen memutuskan untuk tidak mempunyai anak. Kata Amy, anak-anak itu berisik, rewel dan tidak tahu aturan. Tapi, jam biologis yang terus berdetak, membuat Amy berpikir. Usianya sudah kepala 3, bisa-bisa jika suatu saat dia memutuskan untuk punya anak, anaknya mungkin tidak akan mengenal orang tuanya apalagi kakek-neneknya.<br /><br />Maka mulailah program baru Amy yaitu hamil. Dan ketika akhirnya Amy pun hamil, kembali Amy membuat daftar yang dibutuhkan untuk m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4930606708071853208">Di awal-awal pernikahannya, pasangan Amy dan Stephen memutuskan untuk tidak mempunyai anak. Kata Amy, anak-anak itu berisik, rewel dan tidak tahu aturan. Tapi, jam biologis yang terus berdetak, membuat Amy berpikir. Usianya sudah kepala 3, bisa-bisa jika suatu saat dia memutuskan untuk punya anak, anaknya mungkin tidak akan mengenal orang tuanya apalagi kakek-neneknya.<br /><br />Maka mulailah program baru Amy yaitu hamil. Dan ketika akhirnya Amy pun hamil, kembali Amy membuat daftar yang dibutuhkan untuk menyambut sang bayi. Dibantu buku Baby How, Baby Now, Amy mencoba menghadapi masalah-masalah dalam kehamilan dengan cool.<br /><br />Kehebohan pun timbul, misalnya mengalami morning sickness, indera penciuman yang tiba-tiba jadi super sensitif, mencari tahu apa sih artinya layette, mencari nama untuk calon bayi, belum lagi menghadapi dua sahabatnya yang aneh – Mandy, yang ‘menentang’ untuk punya anak, dan Anita, yang justru pergi ke bank sperma untuk bisa hamil dan jadi orang tua tunggal.<br /><br />Amy menuturkan hari-harinya dengan kocak di dalam buku hariannya, sampai bagaimana perasaannya yang haru bahagia ketika menggendong bayi mungilnya. Di detik-detik terakhir pun, Amy masih keras kepala, agar bayinya tidak lahir di saat April Mop.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer6682498">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15462392902731547262">Mumpung lagi hamil juga, wiken kemarin gue beli buku ini. Bacanya cuma butuh waktu 2 hari aja.. karena ga ribet2 banget bukunya. Sebenernya pas kapan gue udah kepengin beli buku ini, karena perkiraan gue ini buku pasti lucu. Dan ternyata bener, emang lucu hehe...<br /><br />Tokohnya Amy Thomas Stewart, umurnya ya segue lah (bedanya gue lagi hamil anak kedua aja hehehe..).. Di tengah depresinya dia nyari kerja, terus akhirnya dapet juga, dia tiba2 aja pengin punya anak. Dengan segala macem cara akhirnya dia</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15462392902731547262">Mumpung lagi hamil juga, wiken kemarin gue beli buku ini. Bacanya cuma butuh waktu 2 hari aja.. karena ga ribet2 banget bukunya. Sebenernya pas kapan gue udah kepengin beli buku ini, karena perkiraan gue ini buku pasti lucu. Dan ternyata bener, emang lucu hehe...<br /><br />Tokohnya Amy Thomas Stewart, umurnya ya segue lah (bedanya gue lagi hamil anak kedua aja hehehe..).. Di tengah depresinya dia nyari kerja, terus akhirnya dapet juga, dia tiba2 aja pengin punya anak. Dengan segala macem cara akhirnya dia bisa hamil, dan pas hamil itu dia baru deh ngerasain yang namanya mo jadi ibu tuh gimana. Dengan pegangan buku "sakti" Baby How, Baby Now, dia awalnya merasa pede banget tuh menjalani kehamilannya. Sampe akhirnya.. pengalaman kayaknya mengajarkan dia yang lebih baik ya..<br /><br />Ini buku seru juga dibaca sama ibu2 hamil, terutama sih ibu hamil anak pertama. Kalau buat gue sendiri lebih nggak ngefek ya di saat ini, karena udah ngerti banget dari pengalaman hamil anak pertama. Cuma yang agak sedikit mengganjal itu adalah penanggalan 31 November yang nongol tanpa rasa bersalah aja di buku itu (buku novel ini emang berbentuk jurnal). Bo... 31 November? Sejak kapannn....?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10784376881261474431">First Laura Wolf gave us a hilarious look into the mind of the to do list crazy Amy Thomas as she planned her wedding and drove her fiance and family crazy.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText10784376881261474431">First Laura Wolf gave us a hilarious look into the mind of the to do list crazy Amy Thomas as she planned her wedding and drove her fiance and family crazy. Now in 'DIARY OF A MAD MOM-TO-BE' Amy is back and just as to do list crazy as ever, however, now she is hormonal to boot!<br /><br />Amy is enjoying her life with her now husband of two years Steven just the way it is until one day at a family dinner it hits her..."I want a baby!" From there, trying to conceive all the way to delivery is a hilarious ride for fans of the series as we watch Amy tackle pregnancy in the work place, keeping up friendships and trying to fit in with the "Mommy Set".<br /><br />I think women from all walks of life will enjoy this book from the single girl to the grandmother and everyone in between!<br /></span>

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('G1aMeFpVDYjsT7iRiLnYQ/ss5/gMEpc/nMct7kROJix+grOrqIcZcmCXzCr22D7xstsk4UXP0JX2zih8iNvQaQ==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

They throw themselves and all of their energy and resources into full-time child rearing, turning their kids into the unwitting pawns in a game where success is measured in precocious achievements, jam-packed schedules, and elite private-school pedigrees.Hannah Allen has recently moved to the neighborhood with her New York City–bred investment banker husband and their two-year-old daughter, Violet.
